<p><b>"Baby Boy"</b> is a song by American singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a> from her debut solo studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Dangerously_in_Love" title="Dangerously in Love">Dangerously in Love</a></i> (2003). It features Jamaican singer <a href="/wiki/Sean_Paul" title="Sean Paul">Sean Paul</a> and is also on his <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a>-winning album <i><a href="/wiki/Dutty_Rock" title="Dutty Rock">Dutty Rock</a>,</i> which was re-released in 2003. The artists co-wrote the song with <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" class="mw-redirect" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>, Robert Waller, and <a href="/wiki/Scott_Storch" title="Scott Storch">Scott Storch</a>; the latter is also the producer. Containing a lyrical interpolation of "No Fear" by <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a> group <a href="/wiki/Originoo_Gunn_Clappaz" class="mw-redirect" title="Originoo Gunn Clappaz">O.G.C</a>, "Baby Boy" is an <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dancehall" title="Dancehall">dancehall</a> song with <a href="/wiki/Reggae_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Reggae music">reggae</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arabic_music" title="Arabic music">Arabic music</a> influences; its lyrics detail a woman's fantasies.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Columbia_Records" title="Columbia Records">Columbia Records</a> released "Baby Boy" as the second single from <i>Dangerously in Love</i> to United States radios on August 3, 2003. "Baby Boy" topped the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> chart for nine consecutive weeks, and was Beyoncé's longest-running solo number-one single until 2007. It reached the top ten in many countries, and was certified platinum in Australia and the US.</p>
<p>The song's music video was directed by <a href="/wiki/Jake_Nava" title="Jake Nava">Jake Nava</a> and mostly shows Beyoncé dancing in various locations. "Baby Boy" has remained a staple of Beyoncé's concert <a href="/wiki/Set_list" title="Set list">set list</a>. The <a href="/wiki/American_Society_of_Composers,_Authors_and_Publishers" title="American Society of Composers, Authors and Publishers">American Society of Composers, Authors, and Publishers</a> (ASCAP) recognized it as one of the most performed songs of 2005. During the same year, US singer-songwriter Jennifer Armour filed a <a href="/wiki/Copyright_infringement" title="Copyright infringement">copyright infringement</a> lawsuit claiming that the song had used the primary musical <a href="/wiki/Hook_(music)" title="Hook (music)">hook</a> from her song "Got a Little Bit of Love for You". The suit was dismissed.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background_and_writing">Background and writing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baby_Boy_(Beyonc%C3%A9_song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background and writing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SeanPaul2005.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/SeanPaul2005.jpg/220px-SeanPaul2005.jpg" width="220" height="317" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/SeanPaul2005.jpg/330px-SeanPaul2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/SeanPaul2005.jpg/440px-SeanPaul2005.jpg 2x" data-file-width="753" data-file-height="1085" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SeanPaul2005.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Sean_Paul" title="Sean Paul">Sean Paul</a> contributed vocals to "Baby Boy."</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2002, Beyoncé went to <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>, in the United States, to work with American record producer <a href="/wiki/Scott_Storch" title="Scott Storch">Scott Storch</a> for her debut solo album, <i><a href="/wiki/Dangerously_in_Love" title="Dangerously in Love">Dangerously in Love</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-liner_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-liner-1">[1]</a></sup> She and Storch wrote "Baby Boy", with contributions from American songwriter Robert Waller and Beyoncé's then-boyfriend, <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a> artist <a href="/wiki/Jay_Z" title="Jay Z">Jay Z</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-liner_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-liner-1">[1]</a></sup> The song also contains a lyrical interpolation of "No Fear" by hip hop group <a href="/wiki/Originoo_Gunn_Clappaz" class="mw-redirect" title="Originoo Gunn Clappaz">O.G.C.</a> used towards the ending of the song: "We steppin' in hotter this year".<sup id="cite_ref-Docu_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Docu-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>Once the track was supposedly done, Beyoncé had the idea that it would be "perfect" if <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaican</a> <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">reggae</a> artist <a href="/wiki/Sean_Paul" title="Sean Paul">Sean Paul</a> contributed a vocal track.<sup id="cite_ref-Docu_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Docu-2">[2]</a></sup> Beyoncé contacted Paul about a possible collaboration for "Baby Boy".<sup id="cite_ref-Gil_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gil-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Thread_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thread-4">[4]</a></sup> Sean Paul agreed, and flew in from Jamaica to join the recording sessions of the song.<sup id="cite_ref-Docu_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Docu-2">[2]</a></sup> He contributed a <a href="/wiki/Deejay_(Jamaican)" title="Deejay (Jamaican)">toast</a> verse, and they finished recording "Baby Boy" in March 2003, during the later stages of the album's recording.<sup id="cite_ref-Gil_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gil-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_theme">Music and theme</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baby_Boy_(Beyonc%C3%A9_song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Music and theme">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table role="presentation" class="mbox-small-left" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;float:left">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div class="center">
<div class="floatnone"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" width="50" height="50" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="160" data-file-height="160" /></div>
</div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em">
<div class="haudio">
<div style="padding:4px 0"><a href="/wiki/File:BabyBoySample.ogg" class="mw-redirect" title="File:BabyBoySample.ogg">"Baby Boy"</a></div>
<div>
<div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio id="mwe_player_0" controls="" preload="none" style="width:220px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="22.0580625" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="Baby_Boy_(Beyoncé_song_-_sample).ogg" data-mwprovider="local">
<source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/8/88/Baby_Boy_%28Beyonc%C3%A9_song_-_sample%29.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file (58 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="58159" /></audio></div>
</div>
<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">"Baby Boy" is a hybrid of R&amp;B and dancehall with influences of reggae, house and Arabic music.</div>
</div>
<hr /></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" class="mbox-text" style="line-height:1.1em"><span><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>"Baby Boy" is a <a href="/wiki/Tempo" title="Tempo">midtempo</a> <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">contemporary R&amp;B</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dancehall" title="Dancehall">dancehall</a> song<sup id="cite_ref-Sheetmusicplus_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sheetmusicplus-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Nichols_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nichols-6">[6]</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">reggae</a>, <a href="/wiki/House_music" title="House music">house</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arab_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab people">Arabian music</a> influences.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NME_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NME-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> It was composed using <a href="/wiki/Time_signature" title="Time signature">common time</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Key_(music)" title="Key (music)">key</a> of <a href="/wiki/C_minor" title="C minor">C minor</a>, and set in moderate <a href="/wiki/Groove_(music)" title="Groove (music)">groove</a> of 92 <a href="/wiki/Tempo" title="Tempo">beats per minute</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Sheetmusicplus_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sheetmusicplus-5">[5]</a></sup> Storch's knowledge on <a href="/wiki/Music_of_India" title="Music of India">Indian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Middle_Eastern_music" title="Middle Eastern music">Middle Eastern music</a> contributes to its <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Asia" title="Music of Asia">Eastern</a> influences.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Neil_Drumming" title="Neil Drumming">Neil Drumming</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> noted that "'Baby Boy' goes full-tilt <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">Bollywood</a> 'n da hood, with Sean Paul ripping a pulsing <a href="/wiki/Tabla" title="Tabla">tabla</a> <a href="/wiki/Raga" title="Raga">raga</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Beyoncé's vocals are accompanied by clicky and <a href="/wiki/Castanet" class="mw-redirect" title="Castanet">castanet</a>-sounding <a href="/wiki/Beat_(music)" title="Beat (music)">beats</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Times_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times-12">[12]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Synthesizer" title="Synthesizer">synthesized</a> <a href="/wiki/Clapping" title="Clapping">handclaps</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slapping_(music)" title="Slapping (music)">slaps</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-yahoo_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yahoo-13">[13]</a></sup> According to Roger Friedman of <a href="/wiki/Fox_News_Channel" class="mw-redirect" title="Fox News Channel">Fox News Channel</a>, "Baby Boy" is based on the 1995 reggae song "<a href="/wiki/Here_Comes_the_Hotstepper" title="Here Comes the Hotstepper">Here Comes the Hotstepper</a>", performed by Jamaican singer <a href="/wiki/Ini_Kamoze" title="Ini Kamoze">Ini Kamoze</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>"Baby Boy" is considered to be a sequel in ways to "<a href="/wiki/%2703_Bonnie_%26_Clyde" title="'03 Bonnie &amp; Clyde">'03 Bonnie &amp; Clyde</a>"; a 2002 Jay-Z song featuring Beyoncé.<sup id="cite_ref-Gil_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gil-3">[3]</a></sup> The lyrics detail a woman's fantasies, and in keeping with the album's overall theme, Beyoncé's deemed them as personal to her.<sup id="cite_ref-Thread_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thread-4">[4]</a></sup> Paul remarked, "She's telling me about her fantasies and picturing me and her going here and there, all over the world&#160;... I'm answering back, like, 'I'm wit it'."<sup id="cite_ref-Gil_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gil-3">[3]</a></sup> The lyrics are constructed in the toast–chorus–verse form; Sean Paul performs the toasting while Beyoncé sings all other <a href="/wiki/Song_structure_(popular_music)" class="mw-redirect" title="Song structure (popular music)">verses</a> and <a href="/wiki/Refrain" title="Refrain">choruses</a>. The pattern is repeated twice; a further chorus and verse follow, resolving at the toasting and final verse.<sup id="cite_ref-Docu_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Docu-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release_and_reception">Release and reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baby_Boy_(Beyonc%C3%A9_song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Release and reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Beyonce_Baby_Boy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Two men and a woman are looking forward. Both men are wearing military-style clothing, while the woman is holding a microphone. She wears gypsy-style clothing. In the background, many musical instruments are visible." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Beyonce_Baby_Boy.jpg/200px-Beyonce_Baby_Boy.jpg" width="200" height="181" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Beyonce_Baby_Boy.jpg/300px-Beyonce_Baby_Boy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Beyonce_Baby_Boy.jpg/400px-Beyonce_Baby_Boy.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="579" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Beyonce_Baby_Boy.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Beyoncé singing "Baby Boy" during <a href="/wiki/The_Beyonc%C3%A9_Experience" title="The Beyoncé Experience">The Beyoncé Experience</a> in 2007, flanked by two dancers</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>"Baby Boy" was released as the second single from the debut studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Dangerously_in_Love" title="Dangerously in Love">Dangerously in Love</a></i>. It was added to United States <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_hit_radio" title="Contemporary hit radio">contemporary hit radios</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rhythmic_contemporary" title="Rhythmic contemporary">rhythmic contemporary radios</a> playlists on August 3, 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-rhythmic_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rhythmic-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pop2_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pop2-16">[16]</a></sup> The song was released in <a href="/wiki/Maxi_single" title="Maxi single">maxi single</a> in Canada on October 7, 2003,<sup id="cite_ref-Can_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Can-17">[17]</a></sup> and as a <a href="/wiki/Compact_Disc_single" class="mw-redirect" title="Compact Disc single">CD single</a> in Germany<sup id="cite_ref-Ama.ger_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ama.ger-18">[18]</a></sup> and in the US on October 13, and October 14, 2003 respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> "Baby Boy" was included in the revamped version of Paul's second album, <i><a href="/wiki/Dutty_Rock" title="Dutty Rock">Dutty Rock</a></i> (2003).<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> magazine reviewer Anthony DeCurtis wrote that Beyoncé sounded as if she was "having fun" on the song,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Thomas_Erlewine" title="Stephen Thomas Erlewine">Stephen Thomas Erlewine</a> of the online music guide service <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a> described Beyoncé's vocals as "assured and sexy".<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mark_Anthony_Neal" title="Mark Anthony Neal">Mark Anthony Neal</a> of the international <a href="/wiki/Online_magazine" title="Online magazine">webzine</a> <a href="/wiki/PopMatters" title="PopMatters">PopMatters</a>, regarded "Baby Boy" as one of the "high-profile collaborations" on <i>Dangerously in Love</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Lisa Verrico of the daily British newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i> described the song a "<a href="/wiki/Latino_(demonym)" class="mw-redirect" title="Latino (demonym)">Latino</a>-tinged collaboration ... Paul does a reggae rap in the middle, but it's when he chats while Beyoncé half raps that the pair have real chemistry".<sup id="cite_ref-Times_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times-12">[12]</a></sup> Yancey Strickler of the <i><a href="/wiki/Flak_Magazine" title="Flak Magazine">Flak</a></i> magazine wrote that "'Baby Boy''s <a href="/wiki/Diwali" title="Diwali">diwali</a> stutter is enhanced by Sean Paul's dancehall monotone".<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>James Anthony of the British newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> commented that the track "bridges the gap between the genres of R&amp;B and dancehall".<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> writer Natalie Nichols wrote that "the ... house-spiced 'Baby Boy' successfully meld[s] [Beyoncé's] breathy cooing with hip, interesting production."<sup id="cite_ref-Nichols_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nichols-6">[6]</a></sup> British record label <a href="/wiki/EMI" title="EMI">EMI</a> was honored by the <a href="/wiki/American_Society_of_Composers,_Authors_and_Publishers" title="American Society of Composers, Authors and Publishers">American Society of Composers, Authors and Publishers (ASCAP)</a> during the 2005 Pop Music Awards as Publisher of the Year for publishing "Baby Boy", among other songs.<sup id="cite_ref-ASCAP_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ASCAP-26">[26]</a></sup> Scott Storch earned Songwriter of the Year at the same event.<sup id="cite_ref-ASCAP_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ASCAP-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Chart_performance">Chart performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baby_Boy_(Beyonc%C3%A9_song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Chart performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>"Baby Boy" attained a positioning on the commercial charts before its <a href="/wiki/Compact_Disc_single" class="mw-redirect" title="Compact Disc single">physical release</a> in the US. The track led to a higher <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> chart placing for <i>Dangerously in Love</i>, and helped the album to attain multi-platinum certification in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> The single debuted on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, the official singles chart of America, at number fifty-seven, while "Crazy in Love" was still in the top spot.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> "Baby Boy" dominated the US airplays, and ultimately reaching the top of the Hot 100.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Martens2_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Martens2-30">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Martens3_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Martens3-31">[31]</a></sup> It reached the chart's top spot eight weeks after its debut, and stayed there for nine consecutive weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-Martens3_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Martens3-31">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Martens_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Martens-32">[32]</a></sup> The single stayed number one for a week longer than "Crazy in Love" had, becoming Beyoncé's longest-charting number-one single. The feat was not broken until Beyoncé's 2006 single "<a href="/wiki/Irreplaceable" title="Irreplaceable">Irreplaceable</a>", from her second album <i><a href="/wiki/B%27Day_(Beyonc%C3%A9_album)" title="B'Day (Beyoncé album)">B'Day</a></i> (2006), which spent ten weeks at the top spot in late 2006 to early 2007 due to heavy radio play.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> "Baby Boy" stayed on the Hot&#160;100 for twenty-nine weeks,<sup id="cite_ref-bbbey_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbbey-34">[34]</a></sup> and was certified platinum on June 6, 2006, by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA).<sup id="cite_ref-riaa_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-riaa-35">[35]</a></sup> "Baby Boy" achieved success on <i>Billboard</i> <a href="/wiki/Crossover_(music)" class="mw-redirect" title="Crossover (music)">crossover</a> and mainstream radio charts, appearing on the <a href="/wiki/Top_40_Tracks" title="Top 40 Tracks">Top 40 Tracks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhythmic_contemporary" title="Rhythmic contemporary">Rhythmic Top 40</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mainstream_Top_40_(Pop_Songs)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mainstream Top 40 (Pop Songs)">Top 40 Mainstream</a>, as well as on the <a href="/wiki/Hot_100_Airplay_(Radio_Songs)" title="Hot 100 Airplay (Radio Songs)">Hot 100 Airplay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hot_Dance_Airplay" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot Dance Airplay">Hot Dance Airplay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hot_Dance_Club_Songs" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot Dance Club Songs">Hot Dance Music/Club Play</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BillChartHis_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BillChartHis-37">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AllMusicGuide_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AllMusicGuide-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Martens2_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Martens2-30">[30]</a></sup> As at October 6, 2010, "Baby Boy" had sold 6,000 physical units in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>Internationally, "Baby Boy" performed just as well, peaking inside the top ten on most charts. The single debuted at number two in the United Kingdom, becoming the chart's highest debut and "Baby Boy"'s highest entry internationally.<sup id="cite_ref-uk18_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uk18-40">[40]</a></sup> Though it spent eleven weeks on the chart, it failed to top it (being held off by "<a href="/wiki/Where_Is_the_Love%3F" title="Where Is the Love?">Where Is the Love?</a>" by <a href="/wiki/The_Black_Eyed_Peas" title="The Black Eyed Peas">The Black Eyed Peas</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-uk18_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uk18-40">[40]</a></sup> In most European countries, the single entered the top ten. In Australia and New Zealand, "Baby Boy" peaked at number three and two, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-aus_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aus-41">[41]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rianz_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rianz-42">[42]</a></sup> It was certified platinum by the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Recording_Industry_Association" title="Australian Recording Industry Association">Australian Recording Industry Association</a> for shipment in excess of 70,000 units.<sup id="cite_ref-aria_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aria-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_video">Music video</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baby_Boy_(Beyonc%C3%A9_song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Music video">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Babyboy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A panoramic image of a woman in two different situations. On the left side she is dancing with some people behind her. She is wearing a dark-blue outfit and turquoise shoes. On the other hand, on the image of the right, she is dancing alone and holds a microphone with her hand. She wears dark clothes while she holds her hands in front of her chest." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8f/Babyboy.jpg/190px-Babyboy.jpg" width="190" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8f/Babyboy.jpg/285px-Babyboy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8f/Babyboy.jpg/380px-Babyboy.jpg 2x" data-file-width="439" data-file-height="339" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Babyboy.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Beyoncé performing a routine similar to the one featured in the music video (left) to "Baby Boy"</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Music_video" title="Music video">music video</a> for "Baby Boy" was filmed by English director <a href="/wiki/Jake_Nava" title="Jake Nava">Jake Nava</a>, who also shot Beyoncé's "Crazy in Love" video. It was recorded in <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami, Florida</a> on August 7–8, 2003. Parts of the video were captured in a house with different style rooms: one in a Japanese style and one in an old English style.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>Scenes featuring Beyoncé and Paul are shown separately. The video begins with Paul sitting on a throne while <a href="/wiki/Deejay_(Jamaican)" title="Deejay (Jamaican)">toasting</a>; Beyoncé is leaning against a wall and dancing. In the following scene, Beyoncé is seen on a bed tossing herself. Paul is shown with several women who are lying on the floor caressing each other. Beyoncé walks towards the beach; she spots a man, and the two touch and flirt. As the second verse of the begins, Beyoncé is at a party. At the party Beyoncé decides to dance with the same man that she interacted with earlier. Then, water floods the floor of the party as she sings "the dance floor becomes the sea". As the second chorus of the song begins, the video is cut with scenes of Beyoncé and four back-up dancers dancing on a platform in the sand on the beach. The original track is interrupted towards the end with an <a href="/wiki/Arabic_music" title="Arabic music">Arabic</a> instrumental, designed for the music video. This section showcases Beyoncé vigorously dancing on the sand.</p>
<p>Sal Cinquemani of the online publication <a href="/wiki/Slant_Magazine" title="Slant Magazine">Slant Magazine</a>, described the video as a "baby-oil-logged follow-up" to "Crazy in Love"'s "bootylicous video".<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> In 2013, John Boone and Jennifer Cady of <a href="/wiki/E!_Online" class="mw-redirect" title="E! Online">E! Online</a> placed the video at number nine on their list of Beyoncé's ten best music videos, praising the extended belly-dancing breakdown.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> "Baby Boy" premiered on <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a>'s program <i><a href="/wiki/Total_Request_Live" title="Total Request Live">Total Request Live</a></i> on August 25, 2003 at number ten and reached the top spot.<sup id="cite_ref-TRL_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TRL-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> It stayed on the show for forty-one days, the same chart run "<a href="/wiki/Me,_Myself_and_I_(Beyonc%C3%A9_song)" title="Me, Myself and I (Beyoncé song)">Me, Myself and I</a>" earned.<sup id="cite_ref-TRL_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TRL-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Live_performances">Live performances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baby_Boy_(Beyonc%C3%A9_song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Live performances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Beyonce_at_Montreal_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="An image showing five women wearing black outfits in front of a screen" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Beyonce_at_Montreal_2013.jpg/250px-Beyonce_at_Montreal_2013.jpg" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Beyonce_at_Montreal_2013.jpg/375px-Beyonce_at_Montreal_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Beyonce_at_Montreal_2013.jpg/500px-Beyonce_at_Montreal_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Beyonce_at_Montreal_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Beyoncé performing "Baby Boy" during <a href="/wiki/The_Mrs._Carter_Show_World_Tour" title="The Mrs. Carter Show World Tour">The Mrs. Carter Show World Tour</a>, 2013</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Beyoncé first performed "Baby Boy" live at the 2003 <a href="/wiki/2003_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2003 MTV Video Music Awards">MTV Video Music Awards</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> she sang it in a <a href="/wiki/List_of_musical_medleys" title="List of musical medleys">medley</a> with the pre-recorded vocals of Paul.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Beyoncé later sang "Baby Boy" with Paul at the <a href="/wiki/MTV_Europe_Music_Awards_2003" class="mw-redirect" title="MTV Europe Music Awards 2003">2003 MTV Europe Music Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> "Baby Boy" has been included on the <a href="/wiki/Set_list" title="Set list">set list</a> for most of Beyoncé's concert tours. It served as opening song of her <a href="/wiki/Dangerously_in_Love_Tour" title="Dangerously in Love Tour">Dangerously in Love World Tour</a> that began in late 2003. During her performance of the song on the tour, she was initially suspended from the ceiling of the arena that was gradually lowered to a red lounger—a prop she also used during the 2003 MTV VMAs.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> The footage taken in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Arena" title="Wembley Arena">Wembley Arena</a> in the UK was included on the <i><a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9:_Live_at_Wembley" class="mw-redirect" title="Beyoncé: Live at Wembley">Live at Wembley</a></i> concert DVD. Beyoncé also performed "Baby Boy" with her former group <a href="/wiki/Destiny%27s_Child" title="Destiny's Child">Destiny's Child</a>'s farewell tour <a href="/wiki/Destiny_Fulfilled_..._And_Lovin%27_It" class="mw-redirect" title="Destiny Fulfilled ... And Lovin' It">Destiny Fulfilled ... And Lovin' It</a>, and it was included on the <i><a href="/wiki/Destiny%27s_Child:_Live_in_Atlanta" title="Destiny's Child: Live in Atlanta">Destiny's Child: Live in Atlanta</a></i> concert DVD.<sup id="cite_ref-incor_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-incor-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>"Baby Boy" was a part of Beyoncé's set list on <a href="/wiki/The_Beyonc%C3%A9_Experience" title="The Beyoncé Experience">The Beyoncé Experience</a> in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> and <a href="/wiki/I_Am..._World_Tour" title="I Am... World Tour">I Am... World Tour</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> On August 5, 2007, Beyoncé performed the song at the <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden" title="Madison Square Garden">Madison Square Garden</a> in <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-jiv_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jiv-55">[55]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mui_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mui-56">[56]</a></sup> wearing a belly-dancer-type outfit, she descended the staircase holding an umbrella and was met by three guys wearing fatigues.<sup id="cite_ref-mui_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mui-56">[56]</a></sup> A short section of the reggae classic "Murder She Wrote" was incorporated into "Baby Boy".<sup id="cite_ref-mui_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mui-56">[56]</a></sup> Jon Pareles of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> praised the performance, writing that Beyoncé "needs no distractions from her singing, which can be airy or brassy, tearful or vicious, rapid-fire with staccato syllables or sustained in curlicued melismas. But she was in constant motion, strutting in costumes".<sup id="cite_ref-jiv_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jiv-55">[55]</a></sup> She performed in a similar arrangement at the Los Angeles' <a href="/wiki/Staples_Center" title="Staples Center">Staples Center</a> on September 2, 2007. She was dressed in a belly dancing outfit, and the performance was executed with several male backup dancers and live instrumentation.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Beyoncé re-produced the dance she executed in the song's music video.<sup id="cite_ref-incor_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-incor-53">[53]</a></sup> When Beyoncé performed "Baby Boy" in <a href="/wiki/Sunrise,_Florida" title="Sunrise, Florida">Sunrise, Florida</a> on June 29, 2009, she was wearing a glittery gold leotard. When her performance began, she was suspended in the air, and then lowered to the <a href="/wiki/B-Stage" class="mw-redirect" title="B-Stage">B-Stage</a> to where she sang "Baby Boy" with an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Dawn_Penn" title="Dawn Penn">Dawn Penn</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/You_Don%27t_Love_Me_(No,_No,_No)" title="You Don't Love Me (No, No, No)">You Don't Love Me (No, No, No)</a>". Animated graphics of turntables, faders and other club equipment were projected behind the dancers and musicians.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Beyoncé was accompanied by two drummers, two keyboardists, a percussionist, a horn section, three imposing backup vocalists called the Mamas and a lead guitarist, Bibi McGill.<sup id="cite_ref-Self_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Self-59">[59]</a></sup> "Baby Boy" was included on her live albums <i><a href="/wiki/The_Beyonc%C3%A9_Experience_Live" title="The Beyoncé Experience Live">The Beyoncé Experience Live</a></i> (2007),<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> and the deluxe edition of <i><a href="/wiki/I_Am..._World_Tour" title="I Am... World Tour">I Am... World Tour</a></i> (2010).<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> At the 2005 <a href="/wiki/American_Society_of_Composers,_Authors_and_Publishers" title="American Society of Composers, Authors and Publishers">ASCAP</a> Pop Music Awards, "Baby Boy" along with Beyoncé's two other songs – "Me, Myself and I" and "<a href="/wiki/Naughty_Girl_(Beyonc%C3%A9_song)" title="Naughty Girl (Beyoncé song)">Naughty Girl</a>" – were recognized as three of the most performed songs of 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>"Baby Boy" was performed by Beyoncé in a pink fringe dress at a concert at Palais Nikaïa in Nice, France, on June 20, 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> and at the <a href="/wiki/Glastonbury_Festival_2011" title="Glastonbury Festival 2011">Glastonbury Festival</a> on June 26, 2011, where she brought out British <a href="/wiki/Trip_hop" title="Trip hop">trip hop</a> singer <a href="/wiki/Tricky_(musician)" title="Tricky (musician)">Tricky</a> to guest on the song.<sup id="cite_ref-glastonbury2011_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-glastonbury2011-64">[64]</a></sup> In May, 2012, Beyoncé performed the song during her <i><a href="/wiki/Revel_Presents:_Beyonc%C3%A9_Live" title="Revel Presents: Beyoncé Live">Revel Presents: Beyoncé Live</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Revue" title="Revue">revue</a> in <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_City,_New_Jersey" title="Atlantic City, New Jersey">Atlantic City, New Jersey</a>, United States' <a href="/wiki/Entertainment" title="Entertainment">entertainment</a> <a href="/wiki/Resort" title="Resort">resort</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hotel" title="Hotel">hotel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Casino" title="Casino">casino</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spa" title="Spa">spa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Revel_Atlantic_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Revel Atlantic City">Revel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-spinmag_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spinmag-66">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-village_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-village-67">[67]</a></sup> Jim Farber of the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_News_(New_York)" class="mw-redirect" title="Daily News (New York)">Daily News</a></i> wrote, "The first, and last parts of the show stressed the steeliest Beyoncé, told in bold songs... [like] dancehall-inflected 'Baby Boy.'"<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> On February 3, 2013, Beyoncé performed the song during the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLVII_halftime_show" title="Super Bowl XLVII halftime show">Super Bowl XLVII halftime show</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Copyright_infringement_lawsuit">Copyright infringement lawsuit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Baby_Boy_(Beyonc%C3%A9_song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Copyright infringement lawsuit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2005, US singer-songwriter Jennifer Armour filed a <a href="/wiki/Copyright_infringement" title="Copyright infringement">copyright infringement</a> lawsuit, claiming that Beyoncé had used some lyrics and the musical <a href="/wiki/Hook_(music)" title="Hook (music)">hook</a> from her song "Got a Little Bit of Love for You".<sup id="cite_ref-Fox_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fox-70">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Case_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Case-72">[72]</a></sup> In 2003, Armour's former label manager had submitted a <a href="/wiki/Demo_(music)" title="Demo (music)">demo</a> recordings to <a href="/wiki/Record_label" title="Record label">record labels</a>, including Beyoncé's <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Records" title="Columbia Records">Columbia Records</a> and Sean Paul's <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Records" title="Atlantic Records">Atlantic Records</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IE_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IE-74">[74]</a></sup> According to the district court, an Expert witness (Chair, Dept. of Music Theory &amp; Composition, Shepherd School of Music, Rice University) determined the songs to be "<a href="/wiki/Substantial_similarity" title="Substantial similarity">substantially similar</a>" (a requirement for an infringement finding). With regard to the musical hook, the Expert stated in his report, "When the aural comparisons of the two songs are presented in the key of C Minor (for easy comparison) and presented back-to-back, in A–B–A–B fashion, even the least musically inclined listener should immediately determine that the two songs are strikingly similar; I daresay that many listeners may even perceive them as being the same song! And again, transposing a song for this purpose does not alter any fundamental qualities or characteristics of the song but merely assists the ability of those unfamiliar with the technicalities of music in making a comparison." The district court judge nonetheless ruled that she, herself, could not hear the similarities between the two songs and dismissed the case, denying the motion for the songs or case to be heard by a jury.<sup id="cite_ref-Case_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Case-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>On appeal, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Fifth_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Fifth Circuit">United States Court of Appeals for the Fifth Circuit</a> affirmed the district court's ruling, but ruled with different reasoning. It held that there was no infringement based on Beyoncé's claim that Armour's demo tape was received shortly after the writing of Beyoncé's song had been substantially completed. However, the court did not address the issue of substantial similarity.<sup id="cite_ref-IE_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IE-74">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
